# Wallet Setup for Arbitrum Compatibility | Camelot DEX

Throughout this guide, we will assume that you are using the Metamask wallet since it is the one most people use, the process of setting up a wallet should be very similar regardless of the wallet you choose.

It's worth mentioning that Nitro network settings are the same as Arbitrum One's previous settings.

The easiest way to add Arbitrum to your wallet is through Chainlist. Using the steps below, you can add Arbitrum to your wallet without typing anything manually.

1.  Go to [https://chainlist.org/](https://chainlist.org/)
    
2.  Click ‘Connect Wallet’ upon notification from your wallet click Approve
    

![](https://docs.camelot.exchange/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3420642431-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FHBFQDThxW7Uo7iHfOHG5%252Fuploads%252F4zNkuyixSpHZbeOfcHAv%252F1%2520connect%2520your%2520wallet%2520chainlist.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D08b4da6d-9a42-4570-938a-030671e3c481&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=80d6ec5&sv=2)

3\. Locate Arbitrum One and click Add to metamask

![](https://docs.camelot.exchange/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3420642431-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FHBFQDThxW7Uo7iHfOHG5%252Fuploads%252FU2iGup8EcvMq7Rh0fn4A%252F2%2520Add%2520Arbitrum%2520One%2520to%2520metamask%2520chainlist.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D48aafe2b-c4e5-4654-992b-5a8cd71bc26b&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=97f903cc&sv=2)

4\. Upon notification from your wallet click Approve

![](https://docs.camelot.exchange/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3420642431-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FHBFQDThxW7Uo7iHfOHG5%252Fuploads%252FQMrz9saWkUOXWuVObeAJ%252F3%2520add%2520network%2520chainlist.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D220a5208-70ea-460d-9ebe-6aae1cf74eb9&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=eec7d3ab&sv=2)

5\. In the following popup click Switch network

![](https://docs.camelot.exchange/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3420642431-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FHBFQDThxW7Uo7iHfOHG5%252Fuploads%252FKW5UGngzorcagkxH9Tw4%252F4%2520switch%2520network%2520chainlist.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D99916cf3-26a4-43b2-9c1d-696caf1bb93f&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=14e8ccfb&sv=2)

6\. You can now use the Arbitrum network.

**In case you do not wish to interact with the Chainlist website, you can manually add Arbitrum to your wallet. Below are the steps you need to follow:**

1.  The first step is to open Metamask and select the network icon dropdown menu
    

![](https://docs.camelot.exchange/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3420642431-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FHBFQDThxW7Uo7iHfOHG5%252Fuploads%252FD6ABGweTdiC9n544yQx5%252Fimage.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D0aa3faa6-ef1f-408a-bc5a-d0c0455722d5&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=b6cc22d&sv=2)

2\. When the pop-up appears, click Add Network

![](https://docs.camelot.exchange/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3420642431-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FHBFQDThxW7Uo7iHfOHG5%252Fuploads%252Fen45vYIemd0zt2NSCruX%252Fimage.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D76ef50c3-cbfe-4ceb-ac32-7e472de837a8&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=d4390928&sv=2)

3\. The Add a network page will open. Add the following details:

Network name

Arbitrum One

RPC URL

[https://arb1.arbitrum.io/rpc](https://arb1.arbitrum.io/rpc)

Chain ID

42161

Currency symbol

ETH

Block explorer URL

[https://arbiscan.io/](https://arbiscan.io/)

Network name

Arbitrum One

RPC URL

[https://arbitrum.llamarpc.com/](https://arbitrum.llamarpc.com/)

Chain ID

42161

Currency symbol

ETH

Block explorer URL

[https://arbiscan.io/](https://arbiscan.io/)

![](https://docs.camelot.exchange/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3420642431-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FHBFQDThxW7Uo7iHfOHG5%252Fuploads%252FbVfGjHdKvgDH26xl4uTY%252F33.jpg%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Ddb5038ab-65d6-44e4-a05f-c99cdc51dd52&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=9e42e35f&sv=2)

Once you're finished, click Save

4\. You are now connected to the Arbitrum network

[PreviousWallet Creation](https://docs.camelot.exchange/get-started/arbitrum-guide/wallet-creation)
[NextBridging tokens to Arbitrum](https://docs.camelot.exchange/get-started/arbitrum-guide/bridging-tokens-to-arbitrum)

Last updated 1 year ago

# ⚖️┃Token distribution | Camelot DEX

### 

[](https://docs.camelot.exchange/tokenomics/token-distribution#grail-allocation)

GRAIL allocation

![](https://docs.camelot.exchange/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3420642431-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FHBFQDThxW7Uo7iHfOHG5%252Fuploads%252FFaBG4FburK1iacJSl2n6%252FToken%2520Pie%2520Chart.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D9c11abf0-65ba-4746-a951-7dcf7e114869&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=6daedf6e&sv=2)

#### 

[](https://docs.camelot.exchange/tokenomics/token-distribution#genesis)

Genesis

*   15% to the Public Sale distributed upfront (5% xGRAIL & 10% GRAIL)
    
*   10% to Protocol Owned Liquidity (7.5% used for initial liquidity, pre-minted in a multisig)
    
*   5% to the Genesis Nitro Pools distributed linearly over 6 months as xGRAIL
    

#### 

[](https://docs.camelot.exchange/tokenomics/token-distribution#grail)

GRAIL

*   22.5% to Liquidity Mining over the next 3 years
    
*   20% to the Core Contributors vested linearly over 3 years
    
*   10% to Partnerships (6-months cliff and 2 years vesting)
    
*   8% to Reserves (pre-minted in a multisig)
    
*   5% to Ecosystem
    
*   2.5% to the Development Fund vested linearly over 3 years
    
*   2% to Advisors vested linearly over 3 years
    

_Except Reserves and the Development fund, all emissions are made with a combination of GRAIL and xGRAIL_

### 

[](https://docs.camelot.exchange/tokenomics/token-distribution#grail-supply-release-schedule)

GRAIL supply release schedule

![](https://docs.camelot.exchange/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3420642431-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FHBFQDThxW7Uo7iHfOHG5%252Fuploads%252FF1C6UPZ3ib9xdT1pAvWJ%252Fimage.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D7988d127-95de-453e-a538-65ff1874b412&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=5b9734b6&sv=2)

![](https://docs.camelot.exchange/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3420642431-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FHBFQDThxW7Uo7iHfOHG5%252Fuploads%252FqqkwKLPcSFVt7U84tg7o%252Fimage.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Df0a80030-7f83-44f3-a6b0-68d9ed3864be&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=23ab26f4&sv=2)

![](https://docs.camelot.exchange/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3420642431-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FHBFQDThxW7Uo7iHfOHG5%252Fuploads%252F0V3XssHPWXtyVX9JBObN%252Fimage.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D3c0ba63d-ac2a-4a8d-b476-6e0f6964c94a&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=b922a0e9&sv=2)

23/08/2024

### 

[](https://docs.camelot.exchange/tokenomics/token-distribution#public-sale)

Public sale

The sale offered 15% of the GRAIL supply, with 10% in GRAIL and 5% in xGRAIL.

The public sale proceeds were allocated as follows:

*   50% immediately paired with 7.5% of GRAIL from POL in UNI v2-style liquidity
    
*   30% was directed towards real yield staking
    
*   20% was allocated to the treasury to fund the Operating expenses
    

### 

[](https://docs.camelot.exchange/tokenomics/token-distribution#genesis-liquidity-mining-program)

**Genesis liquidity mining program**

Starting ten days before the public sale commenced and continuing until its conclusion, Camelot opened deposits for the [Genesis](https://docs.camelot.exchange/launch-and-genesis)
 Pools.

Depositors earned emissions in xGRAIL linearly over the 6 months following the public sale.

### 

[](https://docs.camelot.exchange/tokenomics/token-distribution#liquidity-mining-emissions)

**Liquidity mining emissions**

Camelot will release around 15% of liquidity incentives emissions in GRAIL and 85% in xGRAIL.

The ratio earned will differ by pool and the exact emissions rate will respond to demand but target the rate in the release schedule graph.

Both native and riskier pools will generally earn a higher percentage of GRAIL vs xGRAIL.

### 

[](https://docs.camelot.exchange/tokenomics/token-distribution#partnerships)

Partnerships

The partnership allocation was designated for protocols integrating with Camelot to ensure long-term alignment within the Arbitrum ecosystem.

All partnerships vested over a 2.5-year horizon in xGRAIL with a 6-month cliff.

Most partners served as initial launch partners, with their tokens featured in the Genesis Pools.

[Next🏦┃Protocol earnings](https://docs.camelot.exchange/tokenomics/protocol-earnings)

Last updated 1 year ago

# 🎁┃Incentive system | Camelot DEX

Camelot’s in-house incentive system, offering a robust, efficient, and user-friendly way to distribute rewards to liquidity providers. Built entirely by Camelot, this system integrates on-chain and off-chain components to provide flexibility for protocols and users to create custom campaigns tailored to their specific needs

### 

[](https://docs.camelot.exchange/protocol/incentive-system#key-features)

Key Features

*   **Unified Incentive Distribution**
    
    *   Supports v2 and v3 (with plans to support v4/Integral in the future)
        
    
*   **Permissionless**
    
    *   Any protocol can leverage the system, and it supports all tokens, including GRAIL and xGRAIL
        
    
*   **Highly Customizable Campaigns**
    
    *   Features include Blacklist/Whitelist modes, token weight adjustments, depth-based incentives, and the flexibility to evolve over time
        
    
*   **Deep Partners Integration**
    
    *   Seamlessly functions with Advanced Liquidity Managers (ALMs) and is compatible with any protocol providing liquidity to Camelot, ensuring the best possible user experience for their users
        
    
*   **Streamlines reward collection**
    
    *   Unifies the harvesting of all incentives and emissions into one simple step
        
    
    ![](https://docs.camelot.exchange/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3420642431-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FHBFQDThxW7Uo7iHfOHG5%252Fuploads%252FQO4qy88AdwGNK1b4fUSz%252Fimage.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D434b3bbd-a7ff-42b9-b185-b63184ab310c&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=fb0d8a00&sv=2)
    

### 

[](https://docs.camelot.exchange/protocol/incentive-system#how-the-system-works)

How the System Works

The system is designed to handle reward distribution efficiently while allowing protocols to customize their campaigns

![](https://docs.camelot.exchange/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3420642431-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FHBFQDThxW7Uo7iHfOHG5%252Fuploads%252Fsuh8fQFxaq7lOCEAoPtP%252FOffchain%2520worker%2520computing%2520LP%2520rewards%2520for%2520all%2520campaigns%2520every%2520%7E4%2520hours..png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D438ef3d6-8d7b-4ff5-9f5d-267010db13e4&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=faaba9d5&sv=2)

For instructions on setting up a campaign, refer to the [campaign creation guide](https://docs.camelot.exchange/protocol/incentive-system/campaign-creation)

#### 

[](https://docs.camelot.exchange/protocol/incentive-system#summary-explanation)

**Summary Explanation**

*   Campaigns are created and funds are fully managed on-chain
    
*   An off-chain script computes rewards for LPs
    
    *   The script operates in 4-hour epochs, calculating rewards based on criteria specified during campaign creation
        
    *   After each epoch, it generates a new Merkle root and corresponding proofs, which are uploaded on-chain
        
    
*   **Users can:**
    
    *   Retrieve their Merkle proofs for eligible positions via our API
        
    *   Claim pending rewards from the distributor contract at any time
        
    

#### 

[](https://docs.camelot.exchange/protocol/incentive-system#rewards-eligibility-and-distribution)

**Rewards Eligibility and Distribution**

Users simply need to provide liquidity to be eligible for rewards - no further action is required

*   **V2 Pools**
    
    *   Rewards are distributed proportionally to liquidity ownership
        
    
*   **V3 Pools**
    
    *   Rewards are distributed based on the exact amount of fees generated during an epoch
        
    *   Unlike similar solutions, Camelot computes the precise fees generated for every position in every epoch, ensuring:
        
        *   Extreme accuracy in reward calculations
            
        *   Prevention of cheating or gaming the system
            
        
    

**Example**: A user provides liquidity to the ETH/USDC pool

*   **V2 Pools**: The user owns 1% of the pool’s liquidity and receives 1% of the rewards.
    
*   **V3 Pools**: The user generates 2% of the fees and earns 2% of the rewards
    

#### 

[](https://docs.camelot.exchange/protocol/incentive-system#campaigns-customization)

**Campaigns Customization**

*   **Blacklist/Whitelist Modes**
    
    *   (V2 and V3) Use a blacklist to exclude specific addresses or a whitelist to include only specific addresses
        
    
*   **Token Weighting**
    
    *   (V3 only) Assign weights to specific tokens, allowing rewards to depend not just on fees generated but also on the token composition of the position - this helps incentivize positions that hold more of one token over the other
        
    
*   **Depth Criteria (WIP)**
    
    *   (V3 only) Incentivize or exclude positions based on price ranges
        
    *   Use minimum or maximum liquidity depth to target specific ranges
        
    

A campaign for the BOOP/USDC pool with weights: **Fees = 70%**, **TokenA (BOOP) = 20%**, and **TokenB (USDC) = 10%**, allowing rewards to depend not just on fees but also on token holdings, incentivizing positions with more BOOP

#### 

[](https://docs.camelot.exchange/protocol/incentive-system#campaign-fees-and-requirements)

**Campaign Fees and Requirements**

*   Tokens must be whitelisted to be used in campaigns
    
*   Campaigns must run for at least **24 hours**
    
*   Campaigns must distribute at least **~$50/day** to be considered valid
    
*   A **1% fee** is deducted from the rewards to cover infrastructure costs
    

A protocol creates a campaign to incentivize the GRAIL/ETH pool. They choose already whitelisted USDC as the reward token. The campaign is set to run for 7 days, distributing $500 total, meeting the ~$50/day requirement. A 1% fee is deducted, leaving $495 to be distributed among liquidity providers

### 

[](https://docs.camelot.exchange/protocol/incentive-system#partners-and-integrations)

**Partners and Integrations**

*   **Advanced Liquidity Managers**
    
    *   Users providing liquidity to Camelot through integrated ALMs will receive rewards transparently and directly
        
    *   **Currently Integrated ALMs**:
        
        *   Gamma
            
        *   Jones
            
        *   Beefy (WIP)
            
        *   Steer (WIP)
            
        
    

**Example**: A user provides liquidity to Camelot through Gamma (an integrated ALM). The system automatically tracks their position, and rewards are distributed directly to their wallet without the need for a manual claim

### 

[](https://docs.camelot.exchange/protocol/incentive-system#spnfts-migration)

spNFTs Migration

*   Users holding liquidity in **spNFTs** will continue receiving rewards during the first month to ensure a smooth transition
    
*   spNFT rewards will stop on **January 1st**
    
*   Rewards won’t apply if the spNFT is part of a **Nitro Pool**
    

We strongly encourage migrating liquidity from spNFTs before the deadline

![](https://docs.camelot.exchange/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3420642431-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FHBFQDThxW7Uo7iHfOHG5%252Fuploads%252F6LrUdRVMqYgTAGrffXJa%252Fimage.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Dafd96093-7156-44bd-88db-defae7308e44&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=9a5b02af&sv=2)

[Previous🌐┃AMM V4](https://docs.camelot.exchange/protocol/amm-v4)
[NextCampaign creation](https://docs.camelot.exchange/protocol/incentive-system/campaign-creation)

Last updated 8 months ago

# Campaign creation | Camelot DEX

### 

[](https://docs.camelot.exchange/protocol/incentive-system/campaign-creation#visit-the-campaign-creation-page)

**Visit the Campaign Creation Page**

1.  Go to the [**Camelot dApp**](https://app.camelot.exchange/)
    
2.  Navigate to the **Ecosystem** section at the bottom of the page
    
3.  Click on **Create a Campaign** to access the creation interface
    

![](https://docs.camelot.exchange/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3420642431-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FHBFQDThxW7Uo7iHfOHG5%252Fuploads%252FbKzSQridbCaTQHFDdF0c%252Fimage.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D3840c6ee-62fe-4e89-880a-bf6fb22314a3&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=2dd5d136&sv=2)

### 

[](https://docs.camelot.exchange/protocol/incentive-system/campaign-creation#fill-out-campaign-details)

**Fill Out Campaign Details**

#### 

[](https://docs.camelot.exchange/protocol/incentive-system/campaign-creation#id-1.-select-amm-mode)

**1\. Select AMM mode**

![](https://docs.camelot.exchange/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3420642431-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FHBFQDThxW7Uo7iHfOHG5%252Fuploads%252FWIFLLRHV4mZBGxp2E1DV%252Fimage.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D8d5c3e6c-7142-4f0a-8b2e-9537c655696e&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=cdb04d04&sv=2)

#### 

[](https://docs.camelot.exchange/protocol/incentive-system/campaign-creation#id-2.-select-pool-address)

**2\. Select Pool Address**

*   **Enter or Select**: Manually input the pool address or choose one from the dropdown list provided
    

![](https://docs.camelot.exchange/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3420642431-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FHBFQDThxW7Uo7iHfOHG5%252Fuploads%252F0DQWF0veOACFyIcFPfPO%252Fimage.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D11d4d955-beb0-4e15-aa54-ced32ea701dd&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=16b1ad97&sv=2)

#### 

[](https://docs.camelot.exchange/protocol/incentive-system/campaign-creation#id-3.-set-date-range)

**3\. Set Date Range**

*   **Future Date Required**:
    
    *   Start date must be at least 3 **hours in the future**
        
    *   The end time will automatically align with the start time
        
    
*   **Minimum Duration**: Campaigns must run for at least **24 hours**
    

![](https://docs.camelot.exchange/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3420642431-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FHBFQDThxW7Uo7iHfOHG5%252Fuploads%252FVjGen1l5ZpxpwkB8B1fw%252Fimage.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D0c8bfc73-d37d-4e77-af44-9dd69d4b1dcf&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=58072a68&sv=2)

#### 

[](https://docs.camelot.exchange/protocol/incentive-system/campaign-creation#id-4.-specify-rewards-token-and-amount)

**4\. Specify Rewards Token and Amount**

*   **Choose Token and Amount**:
    
    *   Select the reward token from the dropdown (If your desired reward token isn’t listed, [contact us](https://docs.camelot.exchange/contact-us)
         to have it whitelisted before creating your campaign)
        
    *   Enter the reward amount, ensuring it meets the **minimum daily requirement**
        
    

![](https://docs.camelot.exchange/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3420642431-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FHBFQDThxW7Uo7iHfOHG5%252Fuploads%252FxJZDe4PYEvRlz2FO6fkX%252Fimage.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Dde003e20-c4b8-4fad-b843-6ab1aa237b2f&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=4b4dde71&sv=2)

if the minimum daily reward for coin X is 50 tokens and you set the daily reward to only 30 tokens, the campaign will not be validated. This rule ensures that all campaigns meet a baseline value, preventing spam or low-quality campaigns from flooding the platform and maintaining fairness for participants

#### 

[](https://docs.camelot.exchange/protocol/incentive-system/campaign-creation#id-5.-apply-address-restrictions-optional)

**5\. Apply Address Restrictions (Optional)**

*   **Blacklist/Whitelist**:
    
    *   Use **Blacklist Mode** to exclude specific addresses from rewards
        
    *   Use **Whitelist Mode** to restrict rewards to specific addresses only
        
    
    ![](https://docs.camelot.exchange/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3420642431-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FHBFQDThxW7Uo7iHfOHG5%252Fuploads%252FTlCADJPOoHpOXLxxcmZz%252Fimage.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D9506d122-270d-4fa9-99dc-757f9f648506&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=f3a6b15d&sv=2)
    

#### 

[](https://docs.camelot.exchange/protocol/incentive-system/campaign-creation#id-6.-additional-options-optional)

**6\. Additional Options (Optional)**

*   **Customize Fees and Tokens**:
    
    *   Set weights for **Fees**, **TokenA**, and **TokenB** to determine how rewards are distributed:
        
        *   **Fees**: Rewards are distributed based on fees generated by a position
            
        *   **Token A**: distributed based on holdings of token A in a position
            
        *   **Token B**: distributed based on holdings of token B in a position
            
        
    
*   The sum of **Fees**, **Token A**, and **Token B** must always equal **100%**. No more, no less
    

![](https://docs.camelot.exchange/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3420642431-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FHBFQDThxW7Uo7iHfOHG5%252Fuploads%252FloWI5jekUGCPfhGhpfBK%252Fimage.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D5e348072-8cfc-4527-be98-d3d57158fe3b&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=9a4670e8&sv=2)

**Examples**:

1.  **Fees = 100%**: Rewards are based entirely on fees generated. Token holdings have no impact
    
2.  **Fees = 70%, TokenA = 10%, TokenB = 20%**:
    
    *   70% of rewards are based on fees generated
        
    *   10% of rewards are based on token A holdings
        
    *   20% of rewards are based on token B holdings
        
    

### 

[](https://docs.camelot.exchange/protocol/incentive-system/campaign-creation#confirm-and-submit)

**Confirm and Submit**

1.  **Review Inputs**:
    
    *   Double-check all campaign details (pool, token, date range, restrictions, etc.)
        
    
2.  **Confirm**:
    
    *   Approve and confirm the transaction using your connected wallet to finalize the campaign
        
    

![](https://docs.camelot.exchange/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3420642431-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FHBFQDThxW7Uo7iHfOHG5%252Fuploads%252FmUI1Yz2RXaK2Og0Ei45c%252Fimage.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D9742adb2-2242-4106-b3b8-bddd53d2a59e&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=e2d1e17a&sv=2)

![](https://docs.camelot.exchange/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3420642431-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FHBFQDThxW7Uo7iHfOHG5%252Fuploads%252F6fBcfeo4bn7rn9QEAqpn%252Fclipart529971.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D9f1ef693-c7be-4644-ad9f-e55f5fe60ad8&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=c26bc744&sv=2)

![](https://docs.camelot.exchange/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3420642431-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FHBFQDThxW7Uo7iHfOHG5%252Fuploads%252F1GnrEwfaxH6Wx6LF0Mbu%252Fimage.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Dbeb49a9b-1ebe-4137-990b-3f969b5eb7be&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=12669557&sv=2)

Expect a short delay (up to several minutes) for new campaigns to appear on the interface

Campaigns must meet all minimum requirements (e.g., min duration 24h, reward thresholds) to be valid

[Previous🎁┃Incentive system](https://docs.camelot.exchange/protocol/incentive-system)
[Next🧑‍🌾┃Liquidity Provision](https://docs.camelot.exchange/protocol/liquidity-provision)

Last updated 10 months ago

# 📚┃Glossary | Camelot DEX

### 

[](https://docs.camelot.exchange/references/glossary#apr-annual-percentage-rate)

APR (Annual percentage rate)

A year-to-year interest rate that is generated without compounding.

### 

[](https://docs.camelot.exchange/references/glossary#apy-annual-percentage-yield)

APY (Annual percentage yield)

The real rate of return earned on an investment, taking into account the effect of compounding interest. Compounding interest is calculated periodically and the amount is immediately added to the balance.

With r being the period rate and n the number of compounding periods, we can obtain the APY through this formula:

APY\=(1+r/n)n−1​APY = (1+r/n)^n - 1 ​ APY\=(1+r/n)n−1​

### 

[](https://docs.camelot.exchange/references/glossary#audit)

Audit

A smart contract audit is an extensive methodical examination and analysis of a smart contract's code used to interact with a cryptocurrency or blockchain. This process is conducted to discover errors, issues and security vulnerabilities in the code in order to suggest improvements and ways to fix them.

### 

[](https://docs.camelot.exchange/references/glossary#automated-market-maker-amm)

Automated market maker (AMM)

In a decentralized exchange, an automated market maker (AMM) facilitates the buy and sell orders automatically. AMM works by using self-executing computer programs, also known as smart contracts. AMM eliminates the need for an additional participant when making a trade. Buyers and sellers can instead trade directly with an AMM and its algorithm.

### 

[](https://docs.camelot.exchange/references/glossary#arbitrum)

Arbitrum

A layer 2 scaling solution for Ethereum that uses optimistic rollups to improve transaction throughput and reduce gas fees.

### 

[](https://docs.camelot.exchange/references/glossary#arbitrum-one)

Arbitrum One

The main net of Arbitrum, launched on August 31, 2021.

### 

[](https://docs.camelot.exchange/references/glossary#arbitrum-nitro)

Arbitrum Nitro

An upgraded version of the Arbitrum One network, which increased transaction throughput and further reduced fees.

### 

[](https://docs.camelot.exchange/references/glossary#algebra-v1.9)

Algebra V1.9

Tick-based concentrated liquidity AMM, similar to Uniswap V3.

### 

[](https://docs.camelot.exchange/references/glossary#blockchain)

Blockchain

A blockchain is a peer-to-peer ledger of all transactions across a network.

### 

[](https://docs.camelot.exchange/references/glossary#bonding-curve)

Bonding curve

A mathematical curve used by some automated market maker (AMM) protocols to determine the price of tokens based on their supply and demand, often used in decentralized token sales or token minting processes.

### 

[](https://docs.camelot.exchange/references/glossary#bridge)

Bridge

A technology that connects different blockchains, allowing assets to be transferred between them.

### 

[](https://docs.camelot.exchange/references/glossary#block)

Block

A collection of data, including transactions and other information, that is added to a blockchain once it has been verified and cryptographically secured.

### 

[](https://docs.camelot.exchange/references/glossary#buy-back-and-burn)

Buy back & burn

A process where a portion of the cryptocurrency's supply is used to buy back the tokens from the market and then burn (destroy) them, reducing the total supply and applying continuous buying pressure.

### 

[](https://docs.camelot.exchange/references/glossary#cancel-redeem)

Cancel redeem

An option for users to stop the redeeming process at any time, resulting in the retrieval of the initial amount of xGRAIL and no GRAIL being received.

### 

[](https://docs.camelot.exchange/references/glossary#composability)

Composability

The ability of a system or protocol to be combined and interact with other systems or protocols in a modular and flexible manner.

### 

[](https://docs.camelot.exchange/references/glossary#community-nitro-pools)

Community Nitro pools

Nitro Pools that are openly deployed by anyone, not just Camelot or verified partners.

### 

[](https://docs.camelot.exchange/references/glossary#contract-address)

Contract address

The contract address is where the token contract is located or where a smart contract that manages token holders' balances is located.

### 

[](https://docs.camelot.exchange/references/glossary#concentrated-liquidity)

Concentrated liquidity

A (AMM) feature that allows liquidity providers to define custom price ranges for their assets, focusing liquidity within specific price bands.

### 

[](https://docs.camelot.exchange/references/glossary#conversion-ratio)

Conversion ratio

The proportion at which one token or currency can be exchanged for another.

### 

[](https://docs.camelot.exchange/references/glossary#cold-storage)

Cold storage

The practice of keeping private keys for cryptocurrency wallets offline, typically on a hardware device.

### 

[](https://docs.camelot.exchange/references/glossary#core-contributors)

Core contributors

Key members of a project who contribute to its development and growth.

### 

[](https://docs.camelot.exchange/references/glossary#cex-centralized-exchange)

CEX (Centralized exchange)

A cryptocurrency exchange that is operated by a central authority, responsible for managing user funds and facilitating trades between users.

### 

[](https://docs.camelot.exchange/references/glossary#custom-tick-spacing)

Custom tick spacing

A feature in V3 that allows configuring unique tick spacing settings for each liquidity pool

### 

[](https://docs.camelot.exchange/references/glossary#dapp)

dApp

Decentralized Web3 software application that normally runs on a blockchain.

### 

[](https://docs.camelot.exchange/references/glossary#dao-decentralized-autonomous-organization)

DAO (Decentralized autonomous organization)

Governance mechanism where votes make decisions, and where voting rights are most of the time materialized by a governance token (xGRAIL in our case)

### 

[](https://docs.camelot.exchange/references/glossary#deallocation)

Deallocation

The process of withdrawing xGRAIL from a Plugin, potentially triggering a tax or fee.

### 

[](https://docs.camelot.exchange/references/glossary#deallocation-tax)

Deallocation tax

A fee imposed when deallocating xGRAIL from a Plugin, which is expressed as a percentage and automatically burned, further reducing the supply of GRAIL.

### 

[](https://docs.camelot.exchange/references/glossary#defi)

DeFI

Stands for decentralized finance.

### 

[](https://docs.camelot.exchange/references/glossary#dex-decentralized-exchange)

DEX (Decentralized Exchange)

A decentralized exchange (DEX) is a peer-to-peer (P2P) marketplace that connects cryptocurrency buyers and sellers. In contrast to centralized exchanges (CEXs), decentralized platforms are non-custodial, meaning a user remains in control of their private keys when transacting on a DEX platform.

### 

[](https://docs.camelot.exchange/references/glossary#real-yield-staking-plugin)

Real Yield Staking plugin

Handles the allocation of staking rewards to users.

### 

[](https://docs.camelot.exchange/references/glossary#dynamic-directional-fees)

Dynamic directional fees

Provide the flexibility to reward pairs separately based on the volatility or stability of their assets, as well as on the structure of protocols and their own custom needs.

### 

[](https://docs.camelot.exchange/references/glossary#directional-and-dynamic-volatility-fees)

Directional & dynamic volatility fees

A fee structure that automatically adjusts based on the underlying volatility of the assets in a liquidity pool.

### 

[](https://docs.camelot.exchange/references/glossary#emission-rate)

Emission rate

The speed at which new tokens or coins are created and distributed, typically determined by the underlying consensus mechanism.

### 

[](https://docs.camelot.exchange/references/glossary#elastic-supply-token)

Elastic supply token

A token with a supply that automatically adjusts in response to changes in demand or other predetermined factors, aiming to maintain price stability.

### 

[](https://docs.camelot.exchange/references/glossary#erc-20)

**ERC-20**

ERC-20 is the technical standard for fungible tokens created using the Ethereum blockchain.

### 

[](https://docs.camelot.exchange/references/glossary#erc-721)

ERC-721

The ERC-721 (NFT) Token is unique and can have a different value from another Token in the same smart contract.

### 

[](https://docs.camelot.exchange/references/glossary#escrow)

Escrow

A third-party service or smart contract that temporarily holds funds or assets on behalf of two parties during a transaction, releasing them only when the agreed-upon conditions are met.

### 

[](https://docs.camelot.exchange/references/glossary#fair-launch)

Fair Launch

A transparent and equitable token distribution process without preferential treatment for certain participants, such as pre-sales or venture capital investments.

### 

[](https://docs.camelot.exchange/references/glossary#flash-loan)

Flash loan

A DeFi feature that enables users to borrow assets without collateral for a very short period, typically within a single blockchain transaction, with the loan being repaid instantly at the end of the transaction.

### 

[](https://docs.camelot.exchange/references/glossary#fully-diluted-valuation-fdv)

Fully diluted valuation (FDV)

The valuation of a project based on the current price of its token and the total supply of tokens, including those not yet in circulation.

### 

[](https://docs.camelot.exchange/references/glossary#gas-fees)

Gas fees

A gas fee is charged for the facilitation of a transaction on a blockchain network.

### 

[](https://docs.camelot.exchange/references/glossary#genesis-pools)

Genesis Pools

Exclusive farms for early adopters, designed to bootstrap initial liquidity for Camelot before the GRAIL token went live.

### 

[](https://docs.camelot.exchange/references/glossary#governance-and-governance-tokens)

Governance and governance tokens

Governance refers to determining, maintaining, adapting and enforcing the rules of an ecosystem, product, project, or DAO. It specifically refers to the control and use of a Governance token that carries the right to take part in governance processes.

### 

[](https://docs.camelot.exchange/references/glossary#grail)

Grail

The native, liquid token of Camelot, used for farming rewards and other protocol functions.

### 

[](https://docs.camelot.exchange/references/glossary#xgrail)

xGrail

The escrowed, non-transferable token of Camelot, provides access to core Camelot features.

### 

[](https://docs.camelot.exchange/references/glossary#hardcap)

Hardcap

A predetermined maximum limit on the total supply of a cryptocurrency, set by the developers to control inflation and scarcity.

### 

[](https://docs.camelot.exchange/references/glossary#impermanent-loss)

Impermanent Loss

A user may incur an impermanent loss when he or she locks up crypto tokens in a liquidity pool for the purpose of providing liquidity and earning interest, but the token's price changes due to market volatility or other factors.

### 

[](https://docs.camelot.exchange/references/glossary#intermediaries)

Intermediaries

Third-party entities or services that facilitate transactions between two or more parties.

### 

[](https://docs.camelot.exchange/references/glossary#layer2)

Layer 1 & 2 (L1 & L2)

A Layer 2 protocol applies to off-chain networks that are built on top of Layer 1 networks in order to enhance the capabilities of the underlying Layer 1 networks. For example: Ethereum (L1) - Arbitrum (L2)

### 

[](https://docs.camelot.exchange/references/glossary#layer-3)

Layer 3

Layer 3 is an additional layer on top of existing blockchain networks like Layer 1 (e.g., Ethereum) and Layer 2 (e.g., Arbitrum). It is designed to further enhance scalability, privacy, and customization for decentralized applications. Layer 3 solutions, such as Orbit Chains, enable developers to create specialized, application-specific blockchains that can operate with greater efficiency and flexibility, tailored to the unique needs of each project.

### 

[](https://docs.camelot.exchange/references/glossary#launchpad)

Launchpad

A platform allows projects to launch their tokens and bootstrap liquidity in a decentralized and community-driven manner.

### 

[](https://docs.camelot.exchange/references/glossary#limit-orders)

Limit orders

A type of order in which a trader specifies the price at which they are willing to buy or sell an asset, allowing for greater control over trade execution.

### 

[](https://docs.camelot.exchange/references/glossary#liquidity)

Liquidity

The term liquidity refers to the ease with which a token can be converted into another asset without impacting its value. Liquidity measures the circulating supply and how much trading activity there is in exchange. A currency with low supply and/or circulation is said to be illiquid. Low liquidity levels cause market volatility, resulting in spikes in token prices. A high level of liquidity, however, indicates a stable market with few price fluctuations.

### 

[](https://docs.camelot.exchange/references/glossary#liquidity-mining)

Liquidity mining

Liquidity mining involves placing tokens into a DeFi protocol in order to provide liquidity while receiving rewards for the stakes placed.

### 

[](https://docs.camelot.exchange/references/glossary#liquidity-pool)

Liquidity pool

A Liquidity Pool (LP) is a pool of deposited funds used to provide liquidity for smart contracts.

### 

[](https://docs.camelot.exchange/references/glossary#lp-token-and-liquidity-providers)

LP token & Liquidity providers

A Liquidity Pool (LP) is a pool of deposited funds used to provide liquidity for smart contracts. Liquidity providers contribute to the liquidity pools by depositing assets and receiving in exchange a new token representing the share they own of that pool. This token is called a Liquidity Provider (LP) token.

### 

[](https://docs.camelot.exchange/references/glossary#on-chain)

On-chain

Transactions or operations that occur directly on a blockchain network, as opposed to off-chain transactions, which take place outside the main chain through sidechains or Layer-2 solutions.

### 

[](https://docs.camelot.exchange/references/glossary#optimistic-rollup)

Optimistic rollup

A smart contract-based scaling solution that bundles multiple transactions into a single transaction, reducing computation time and gas consumption.

### 

[](https://docs.camelot.exchange/references/glossary#orbit-chains)

Orbit Chains

Orbit Chains are custom, application-specific blockchains built on the Arbitrum tech stack. They are designed to provide enhanced scalability, security, and flexibility for decentralized applications, allowing them to operate with optimized performance tailored to their specific use cases.

### 

[](https://docs.camelot.exchange/references/glossary#oracles)

Oracles

Data providers that connect blockchain networks to real-world information, such as price feeds or other external data, allowing smart contracts to interact with and react to events outside the blockchain.

### 

[](https://docs.camelot.exchange/references/glossary#multisig-wallet)

Multisig wallet

A multisig wallet requires two or more private keys to sign transactions.

### 

[](https://docs.camelot.exchange/references/glossary#mainnet)

Mainnet

A working, fully-functional blockchain is referred to as the mainnet.

### 

[](https://docs.camelot.exchange/references/glossary#market-cap)

Market Cap

The total value of all outstanding tokens or coins of a cryptocurrency, calculated by multiplying the current price by the circulating supply.

### 

[](https://docs.camelot.exchange/references/glossary#pol-project-owned-liquidity)

POL (Project-Owned Liquidity)

Metrics measuring the amount of LP the Camelot DAO treasury owns.

### 

[](https://docs.camelot.exchange/references/glossary#permissionless)

Permissionless

A feature of decentralized networks and platforms that allows anyone to participate without the need for approval or authorization from a central authority.

### 

[](https://docs.camelot.exchange/references/glossary#plugin)

Plugin

A module within the ecosystem that serves a specific function or interacts with the token in a particular way.

### 

[](https://docs.camelot.exchange/references/glossary#protocol)

Protocol

A DeFi protocol is a program or code written on the blockchain that is used for designing DApps. The protocol is represented by DApps that offer peer-to-peer financial services.

### 

[](https://docs.camelot.exchange/references/glossary#price-impact)

Price impact

The effect of a trade on the price of an asset in a liquidity pool, determined by the size of the trade relative to the pool's total liquidity.

### 

[](https://docs.camelot.exchange/references/glossary#real-yield)

Real yield

A term used to describe earnings generated from a protocol's revenue and distributed to token holders.

### 

[](https://docs.camelot.exchange/references/glossary#rebase-token)

Rebase token

A type of cryptocurrency whose supply adjusts automatically based on a predetermined metric, such as the price of another asset, in order to achieve price stability.

### 

[](https://docs.camelot.exchange/references/glossary#redeeming)

Redeeming

The process of exchanging a token or currency for another, with certain conditions applied, such as vesting.

### 

[](https://docs.camelot.exchange/references/glossary#slippage)

Slippage

Slippage refers to a difference in price between buyer and seller expectations. Slippage can lead to a final sale price of the asset that is either more or less than the requested transaction amount.

### 

[](https://docs.camelot.exchange/references/glossary#smart-contract)

Smart contract

The term smart contract refers to a program that is designed to automate the execution, control, or documentation of legally binding events according to a contract or an agreement.

### 

[](https://docs.camelot.exchange/references/glossary#stablecoin)

Stablecoin

A stablecoin is a cryptocurrency that has its value pegged to the value of a stable asset. Stablecoins are most commonly pegged to the US Dollar.

### 

[](https://docs.camelot.exchange/references/glossary#stable-pair)

Stable pair

A type of token pair in which the assets have strongly correlated price movements, often aiming to maintain a 1:1 transfer ratio.

### 

[](https://docs.camelot.exchange/references/glossary#staking)

Staking

The act of depositing tokens into a yield farming protocol.

### 

[](https://docs.camelot.exchange/references/glossary#swap)

Swap

With a swap, you can instantly exchange one token for another without needing to exchange it for fiat currency.

### 

[](https://docs.camelot.exchange/references/glossary#testnet)

Testnet

Testing network for a new product or project, or for possible improvements to an existing product.

### 

[](https://docs.camelot.exchange/references/glossary#tokenomics)

Tokenomics

Among the factors that determine tokenomics are the number of tokens circulating, the maximum token supply, the rate at which tokens are emitted, and the vesting schedule for tokens.

### 

[](https://docs.camelot.exchange/references/glossary#token-allocation)

Token allocation

The distribution plan for a project's tokens, including details on the total supply, initial distribution, and any reserved or locked tokens.

### 

[](https://docs.camelot.exchange/references/glossary#token-burn)

Token Burn

The process of permanently removing a certain amount of tokens from circulation, often with the goal of reducing supply and increasing the value of the remaining tokens.

### 

[](https://docs.camelot.exchange/references/glossary#trade-routing)

Trade routing

The process of finding the most efficient path for a swap between two assets on a decentralized exchange, often involving multiple intermediate trades to minimize slippage and maximize returns.

### 

[](https://docs.camelot.exchange/references/glossary#tge-token-generation-event)

TGE (Token generation event)

An event where a project's tokens are created and distributed to participants, such as an initial coin offering (ICO) or initial DEX offering (IDO).

### 

[](https://docs.camelot.exchange/references/glossary#tvl-total-value-locked)

TVL (Total Value Locked)

This metric represents the sum of all assets deposited in the protocol.

### 

[](https://docs.camelot.exchange/references/glossary#univ2-and-3)

UniV2 & 3

A reference to Uniswap V2 & 3

### 

[](https://docs.camelot.exchange/references/glossary#vault)

Vault

A smart contract-based solution that automates yield farming strategies by pooling user funds, optimizing asset allocation, and distributing rewards.

### 

[](https://docs.camelot.exchange/references/glossary#vesting)

Vesting

A mechanism that locks up tokens or assets for a specified period, releasing them according to a predetermined schedule or after certain conditions are met.

### 

[](https://docs.camelot.exchange/references/glossary#vesting-duration)

Vesting duration

The length of time that tokens or assets are locked up during the vesting process.

### 

[](https://docs.camelot.exchange/references/glossary#volatile-pair)

Volatile pair

A type of token pair in which the assets have uncorrelated or weakly correlated price movements

### 

[](https://docs.camelot.exchange/references/glossary#volatility)

Volatility

A measure of the degree of price fluctuations in a financial instrument.

### 

[](https://docs.camelot.exchange/references/glossary#wrapped-tokens)

Wrapped tokens

Tokenized versions of existing cryptocurrencies that enable cross-chain compatibility, allowing users to interact with different blockchain networks using a single token.

### 

[](https://docs.camelot.exchange/references/glossary#xgrail-plugins)

xGRAIL plugins

Plugins are contracts linked to the xGRAIL contract. In other words, plugins are additional utilities associated with xGRAIL.

### 

[](https://docs.camelot.exchange/references/glossary#yield)

Yield

The yield is the amount earned by staking or depositing an asset in a DeFi platform.

### 

[](https://docs.camelot.exchange/references/glossary#yield-farming)

Yield farming

Yield farming accounts for depositing or staking tokens across DeFi platforms which provide rewards to liquidity providers. You can generate additional value from your assets by farming them.

### 

[](https://docs.camelot.exchange/references/glossary#yield-aggregator)

Yield aggregator

A DeFi platform or tool that automatically allocates user funds to various yield farming opportunities, aiming to optimize returns by constantly monitoring and rebalancing investments.
